# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that handle HTTP/1.1 to HTTP/2 header translation: the header case normalization (lowercase), the pseudo-header injection (:method, :path, :scheme, :authority), and the upgrade header handling.

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Summary

The answer identifies **40 C++ source and header files** across four key areas:

1. **HTTP/1 Codec Layer** (11 files) - Handles parsing, encoding, and formatting of HTTP/1.1 headers with lowercase normalization
2. **HTTP/2 Codec Layer** (8 files) - Manages HTTP/2 frame encoding, NGHttp2 integration, and pseudo-header handling
3. **Core HTTP Infrastructure** (7 files) - Provides header storage (HeaderMapImpl with automatic lowercase), utilities, and transformation functions
4. **Header Validators** (14 files) - Enforces RFC compliance and performs header validation/transformation for both HTTP/1 and HTTP/2

## Key Components

**Header Case Normalization:**
- Implemented via `Http::LowerCaseString` wrapper in `header_map_impl.cc`
- All headers automatically normalized to lowercase on insertion

**Pseudo-Header Injection:**
- `http2_header_validator.cc` validates and injects `:method`, `:path`, `:scheme`, `:authority`, `:protocol`
- `header_validator.cc` provides individual pseudo-header validation functions
- Follows RFC 7540 pseudo-header ordering requirements

**Upgrade Handling:**
- `utility.cc` contains transformation functions: `transformUpgradeRequestFromH1toH2()`, `transformUpgradeResponseFromH1toH2()`, etc.
- Handles WebSocket, CONNECT, and H2C protocol upgrades
- Manages Connection and Upgrade header conversion to pseudo-headers

implementation:\\n- **source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc**: The HeaderMapImpl class stores all header names in lowercase through the Http::LowerCaseString wrapper, ensuring all headers are normalized to lowercase regardless of input case\\n- **source/common/http/http1/header_formatter.cc**: Provides header formatting utilities that maintain lowercase normalization when encoding/decoding HTTP/1 headers\\n- **source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http1_header_validator.cc**: The ServerHttp1HeaderValidator::transformRequestHeaders() and ClientHttp1HeaderValidator::transformResponseHeaders() methods validate and normalize headers according to RFC 9110 and RFC 9112 specifications\\n\\n## Pseudo-Header Injection (:method, :path, :scheme, :authority, :protocol)\\n\\nThe pseudo-header handling is split between HTTP/2 codec and validators:\\n- **source/common/http/http2/codec_impl.cc**: The HTTP/2 codec implementation injects and handles pseudo-headers during frame encoding/decoding. The encodeHeadersBase() method constructs HTTP/2 HEADERS frames with proper pseudo-header placement\\n- **source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http2_header_validator.cc**: The Http2HeaderValidator class implements comprehensive pseudo-header validation in validateRequestHeaders(). The ServerHttp2HeaderValidator::transformRequestHeaders() and ClientHttp2HeaderValidator::transformRequestHeaders() methods handle the injection of :method, :path, :scheme, and :authority pseudo-headers. Special handling for :protocol pseudo-header is included for extended CONNECT requests\\n- **source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/header_validator.cc**: Base class provides validateMethodHeader(), validateSchemeHeader(), validateHostHeader(), and validatePathHeaderCharacters() methods that validate individual pseudo-headers\\n- **source/common/http/utility.h/cc**: Contains transformUpgradeRequestFromH1toH2(), transformUpgradeResponseFromH1toH2(), transformUpgradeRequestFromH2toH1(), and transformUpgradeResponseFromH2toH1() which handle pseudo-header transformation during HTTP/1 \u2194 HTTP/2 conversion\\n\\n## Upgrade Header Handling (WebSocket, CONNECT, H2C)\\n\\nUpgrade transformations are handled at multiple levels:\\n- **source/common/http/utility.cc**: The primary transformation functions (transformUpgradeRequestFromH1toH2, transformUpgradeResponseFromH1toH2, transformUpgradeRequestFromH2toH1, transformUpgradeResponseFromH2toH1) convert between HTTP/1.1 upgrade requests/responses and HTTP/2 extended CONNECT format. These functions manage Connection, Upgrade headers and convert them to HTTP/2 pseudo-headers\\n- **source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http2_header_validator.cc**: Implements upgrade request/response validation and transformation in ServerHttp2HeaderValidator and ClientHttp2HeaderValidator classes. Special handling for extended CONNECT protocol negotiation\\n- **source/common/http/headers.h**: Defines standard upgrade header constants (websocket, h2c, connect-udp, etc.)\\n- **source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/config_overrides.h**: Manages runtime configuration for upgrade handling behavior\\n\\n## Processing Pipeline\\n\\nThe complete header translation pipeline flows as follows:\\n1. HTTP/1 requests are parsed by source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc (using balsa_parser.cc or legacy_parser_impl.cc)\\n2. Raw headers are stored in HeaderMapImpl (source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc) with automatic lowercase normalization\\n3. Headers pass through ServerHttp1HeaderValidator::transformRequestHeaders() (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http1_header_validator.cc) for validation and potential upgrade transformation\\n4. For HTTP/2 upstreams, utility functions in source/common/http/utility.cc perform protocol conversion (transformUpgradeRequestFromH1toH2)\\n5. The HTTP/2 codec in source/common/http/http2/codec_impl.cc receives the transformed headers with pseudo-headers\\n6. ServerHttp2HeaderValidator and ClientHttp2HeaderValidator (source/extensions/http/header_validators/envoy_default/http2_header_validator.cc) validate and finalize pseudo-header placement\\n7. HTTP/2 HEADERS frames are encoded with proper pseudo-header ordering per RFC 7540\\n\\nThe reverse path (HTTP/2 to HTTP/1) follows the same pattern in reverse using transformUpgradeRequestFromH2toH1 and transformUpgradeResponseFromH2toH1.\\n\\nKey architectural features:\\n- **Automatic lowercase normalization** via Http::LowerCaseString in HeaderMapImpl\\n- **RFC compliance** through separate validators for HTTP/1 (RFC 9112) and HTTP/2 (RFC 7540/RFC 9114)\\n- **Extensible validation** via HeaderValidatorFactory and pluggable validator implementations\\n- **Protocol-agnostic internal representation** where HTTP/2 concepts (pseudo-headers) are the canonical form\\n- **Upgrade handling** for WebSocket, CONNECT, and H2C protocols with proper header transformation\"\n}\n",
